Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gods produced the goddess V─Бk; her do animals of every kind utter; may she, V─Бk, theall-gladdening cow, yielding meat and drink, come to us, worthily praised.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The thunder entering into all beings,becomes the speaker of moral truth, eс╣г─Б m─Бdhyamik─Б v─Бk sarvapr─Бс╣Зyantargat─Б dharm─Бbhiv─Бdin─лbhavati; animals of every kind: whether their utterance be articulare or inarticulate

Jamison Brereton

The gods begat goddess Speech. The beasts of all forms speak her. Gladdening, milking out refreshment and nourishment for us, let Speech, the milk-cow, come well praised to us. с│У

Griffith

The Deities generated Vak the Goddess, and animals of every figure speak her.
May she, the Gladdener, yielding food and vigour, the Milch-cow Vak, approach us meetly lauded.

30рдЕрде рддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢реАрдорд╛рд╣ - рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛рдХреН рдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдЧреНрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ рдЕрд╡рд┐рдЪреЗрддрдирд╛рддрд┐ рдЕрдЪреЗрддрдирд╕рджреГрд╢рд╛рдиреНрдореВрдХрд╛рдиреНрдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдиреЛ рд╡рджрдиреНрддреА рдЕрднрд┐рд╡рджрдирдХреНрд╖рдорд╛рдиреНрдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддреА ред рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд░рд╛рд╖реНрдЯреНрд░реА рд░рд╛рд╖реНрдЯреНрд░рдкрджрд╛ рдордиреНрджреНрд░рд╛ рд╣реГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рд╕рддреА рдирд┐рд╖рд╕рд╛рдж рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпреЗ рдХрд░реНрдордгреНрдпреБрдкрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ ред рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдЧреНрджреЗрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд╛рджрд╛рддреН рдЪрддрд╕реНрд░реЛ рджрд┐рдЧреНрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ рдКрд░реНрдЬрдВ рдХреНрд╖реАрд░рд╛рджрд┐рд░рд╕рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдВ рдкрдпрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рдЬрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ рдЪ рджреБрджреБрд╣реЗ рджреБрд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдЧреНрджреЗрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкрд░рдордВ рдкрджрдВ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрдГ рдХреНрд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рд┐рддреН рдЬрдЧрд╛рдо, рдХреБрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рддрджреАрдпрд╕реНрдерд╛рдирдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреБрдВ рди рдХреЛрд╜рдкрд┐ рдХреНрд╖рдо рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen V─Бk, the queen, the gladdener of the gods, sits down (in the sacrifice) uttering things not to beunderstood, she milks water and food for the four quarters (of the earth); whither now is her best portion gone?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Nirukta 11.28: V─Бk here is the thunder; cf. RV 8.69.14; best portion = the rain, which sinks in the earth or istaken up by the sun’s rays

Jamison Brereton

When Speech, saying indistinguishable things, sat down as gladdening ruler of the gods,
she milked out in four (streams) nourishment and milk drinks. Where indeed did the highest of hers go?

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner is understandably reluctant to construe avicetan─Б╠Бni with v├бdant─л, since this attributes unintelligible speech to Speech herself, but his solution, to construe the neut. pl. loosely with niс╣гas─Б╠Бda (тАЬтАж sich bei den unvern├╝nftigen (Gesch├╢pfen) niederliessтАЭ), does not work syntactically. OldenbergтАЩs mythological explanation is preferable.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the possible mythological background of these verses, as adumbrated by Oldenberg, see the published introduction.

Griffith

When, uttering words which no one comprehended, Vak, Queen of Gods, the Gladdener, was seated,
The heaven’s four regions drew forth drink and vigour: now whither hath her noblest portion vanished?

Geldner

Als die sprechende Rede, die wohlklingende Beherrscherin der G├╢tter sich bei den unvern├╝nftigen Gesch├╢pfen niederlie├Я, da lie├Я sie in vier Strahlen Nahrung und Milch aus sich melken. Wohin ist denn ihr bestes Teil gekommen?

Grassmann

Wenn V─Бk [die Stimme], die K├╢nigin der G├╢tter, unverst├дndliche Worte [den Donner] redend sich niedergesetzt hat, die erfreuende; dann melkt sie aus den vier Weltgegenden Milch [Gewitterregen] als Nahrung sich heraus, wohin ist ihr h├╢chster [Scheitel] gestiegen?

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFour are the definite grades of spech; those Brahmaс╣Зas who are wise know them; three, deposited in secret, indicate no meaning; men speak the fourth grade of speech.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Jamison Brereton

Speech is measured in four feet [/quarters]. Brahmins of inspired thinking know these.
They do not set in motion the three that are imprinted in secret; the sons of Manu speak the fourth (foot/quarter) of speech.

Griffith

Speech hath been measured out in four divisions, the Brahmans who have understanding know them.
Three kept in close concealment cause no motion; of speech, men speak only the fourth division.

Geldner

Auf vier Viertel ist die Sprache bemessen; die kennen die nachsinnenden Brahmanen. Die drei Viertel, die geheim gehalten werden, bringen sie nicht in Umlauf. Das vierte Viertel der Sprache reden die Menschen.

Grassmann

Die Rede hat vier abgegrenzte Gattungen; die sind bekannt den Brahmanen, welche weise sind; die drei ins Verborgene gesetzte [die drei Veden?] offenbaren sie nicht; die vierte Gattung der Rede sprechen die Menschen.

Elizarenkova

With trust is the fire kindled; with trust is the oblation poured.
We at the head of good fortune make known our trust with speech.

By Faith is Agni kindled, through Faith is oblation offered up.
We celebrate with praises Faith upon the height of happiness.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬO ┼Ъraddh─Б_, grant the desire of the donor (of the oblation), grant, O ┼Ъraddh─Б, the desire of himwho wishes to give, grant this boon which I have mentioned to my sacrificers who solicit happiness.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Trust, this (speech) spoken by me: make it dear to him who gives, dear to him who intends to give,
and dear among the benefactors who offer sacrifice, o Trust.

Griffith

Bless thou the man who gives, O Faith; Faith, bless the man who fain would give.
Bless thou the liberal worshippers: bless thou the word that I have said.

Geldner

O Glaube! Mache diese meine Rede dem Schenkenden lieb, o Glaube, dem zu schenken Gewillten lieb, den gastfreien Opferern lieb!

Grassmann

O Glaube, lieb mach dieses Wort des Spenders, der noch spenden will, Mach lieb es bei den g├╝tigen, o Glaube, bei den Opferern.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs the gods had faith in (their fight with) the Asuras, so grant the boon which has been asked for toour sacrificers who solicit happiness.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just the gods created trust in themselves among the powerful lords, so among the benefactors who offer sacrifice make what has been spoken by us trust(ed).

Griffith

Even as the Deities maintained Faith in the mighty Asuras,
So make this uttered wish of mine true for the liberal worshippers.

Geldner

Grassmann

Wie G├╢tter der Asurenschar, der starken, schenkten ihr Vertraun, So mache du auch unser Wort vertraut den g├╝t’gen Opferern.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGods, worshippers, and those who are protected by V─Бyu, solicit ┼Ъraddh─Б, (they cherish) ┼Ъraddh─Бwith heartfelt desire, through ┼Ъraddh─Б a man acquires wealth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 8.44; Nirukta 7.2

Jamison Brereton

Trust do the gods revere, sacrificing for themselves with V─Бyu as their herdsmanтАФ
trust, with a purpose that comes from their heart. By trust one gains possession of goods.

Griffith

Guarded by Vayu, Gods and men who sacrifice draw near to Faith.
Man winneth Faith by yearnings of the heart, and opulence by Faith.

Geldner

Den Glauben ehren die opfernden G├╢tter unter Vayu┬┤s Hut, den Glauben mit herzlichem Vorsatz; durch den Glauben gewinnt man Gut.

Grassmann

Den Glauben ehren andachtsvoll die G├╢tter, die der Wind beschirmt; Der Glaube wird durch Herzens Trieb, durch Glauben wird das Gut erlangt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe invoke ┼Ъraddh─Б at dawn, and again at midday, and also at the setting of the sun; inspire us inthis world, ┼Ъraddh─Б, with faith.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Trust do we call early in the morning, trust at midday,
trust at the setting of the sun. O Trust, place a trusting heart
here in us.

Griffith

Faith in the early morning, Faith at noonday will we invocate,
Faith at the setting of the Sun. O Faith, endow us with belief.

Geldner

Den Glauben rufen wir morgens an, den Glauben um Mittag, den Glauben, wann die Sonne untergeht. O Glaube, mach, da├Я man uns hier Glauben und Vertrauen schenke.

Grassmann

Den Glauben rufen Morgens wir, den Glauben in der Mittagszeit Den Glauben, wenn die Sonne sinkt, o Glaube, mache gl├дubig uns.

рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереАред

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)
  • рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпреЛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛
  • рд╡рддреНрд╕рд╛рд░ рдЛрд╖рд┐рдГ
  • рдирд┐рдЪреГрддреНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН
  • рдзреИрд╡рддрдГ
рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдХрд┐рд╕ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛ рдХреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИ рее

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдЯреАрдХрд╛

рдпрджреЗрддрдЬреНрдЬрдЧрддреНрдХрд╛рд░рдгрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо ‘рд╕рддреНрдпрдВ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдордирдиреНрддрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╢реНрд░реБрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдВ рддрджреЗрддрддреН рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрд╛рджреМ рдЬрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рдЬрдЧрджрд╛рдХрд╛рд░реЗрдгреЛрддреНрдкрджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╕рддреН рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рддреН рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдВ рджрд┐рд╢рд┐ рд╡реЗрдирдГ рдХрдордиреАрдп рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпреЛ рднреВрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрд░реБрдЪрдГ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╕реАрдорддрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрдкрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдореЛрджрдЧреНрджрд┐рдЧреНрд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╕реАрдореНрдиреЛ рд╡рд┐рднрдЬреНрдп рдЖрд╡рдГ рдЖрд╡реГрдгреЛрддреН ред рд╕ рд╡реЗрдирдГ рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпреЛ рдмреБрдзреНрдирд┐рдпрд╛рдГ рдмреБрдзреНрдирдВ рдореВрд▓рдВ рддрддреНрд░ рднрд╡рд╛рдГ рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢рд╡рд╛рдпреНрд╡рдЧреНрдирд┐рдЬрд▓рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрдГ рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рднрдЬреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд╛ рдЕрдХрд░реЛрджрд┐рддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╕рддрд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдЧрд┐рд░рд┐рдирджреАрд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рд╛рджреЗрдГ рдЕрд╕рддрд╢реНрдЪ рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдпреЛрдирд┐рдВ рдХрд╛рд░рдгрдВ рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгрдВ рднреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рд░реВрдкрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╡рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╡реГрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдЬрдЧрджреНрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдВ рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ (рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рддреН) рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдХреА рдЖрджрд┐ рдореЗрдВ (рдЬрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН) рд╕рдм рдХрд╛ рдЙрддреНрдкрд╛рджрдХ рдФрд░ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрд╛ (рдкреНрд░рдердордореН) рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдХрд░реНрддрд╛ (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо) рд╕рдм рд╕реЗ рдмрдбрд╝рд╛ рдЬреЛ (рд╕реБрд░реБрдЪрдГ) рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рд░реБрдЪрд┐ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп (рд╡реЗрдирдГ) рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдЬрд┐рд╕ (рдЕрд╕реНрдп) рдЗрд╕ рдХреЗ (рдмреБрдзреНрдиреНрдпрд╛рдГ) рдЬрд▓ рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзреА рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рди рд╕реВрд░реНрдп, рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╛, рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдФрд░ рдирдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░ рдЖрджрд┐ (рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдз рд╕реНрдерд▓реЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд╕реНрдерд┐рдд (рдЙрдкрдорд╛рдГ) рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХреЗ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрдд рд▓реЛрдХ рд╣реИрдВ, рдЙрди рд╕рдм рдХреЛ (рд╕рдГ) рд╡рд╣ (рдЖрд╡рдГ) рдЕрдкрдиреА рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрд┐ рд╕реЗ рдЖрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рджрди рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡рд╣ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ (рд╡рд┐рд╕реАрдорддрдГ) рдорд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рджрд╛ рд╕реЗ (рд╕рддрдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рди рджреЗрдЦрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рдЪ) рдФрд░ (рдЕрд╕рддрдГ) рдЕрд╡реНрдпрдХреНрдд (рдЪ) рдФрд░ рдХрд╛рд░рдг рдХреЗ (рдпреЛрдирд┐рдореН) рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢рд░реВрдк рд╕реНрдерд╛рди рдХреЛ (рд╡рд┐рд╡рдГ) рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЙрд╕реА рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рдХреА рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛ рд╕рдм рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдирд┐рддреНрдп рдЕрд╡рд╢реНрдп рдХрд░рдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реерей рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the cows come and bring good fortune; let them lie down in (our) stalls and be plural ased with us; may the many-coloured kine here be parboiled milk for Indra on many dawns.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The cows have come here and have made (the house) blessed. Let them find a place in the cow-stall; let them find enjoyment among us.
Here should those of many colors be, bearing offspring, as through
many dawns they give milk for Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In p─Бda a тАШhouseтАЩ is supplied as obj. of bhadr├бm akran on the basis of 6c bhadr├бс╣Г gс╣Ыh├бс╣Г kс╣Ыс╣Зutha. Geldner simply тАЬhaben Gl├╝ck gebracht,тАЭ Whitney (AV IV.21.1) тАЬhave done what is excellent,тАЭ and this is certainly possible.

Griffith

THE Kine have come and brought good fortune: let them rest in the cow-pen and be happy near us.
Here let them stay prolific, many-coloured, and yield through many morns their milk for Indra.

Geldner

Die K├╝he sind angekommen und haben Gl├╝ck gebracht. Sie sollen sich im Kuhstall niederlegen und sich bei uns wohl f├╝hlen. Reich an Nachkommenschaft m├╢gen die Buntfarbigen hier sein und viele Morgen f├╝r Indra Milch geben.

Grassmann

Gekommen sind die K├╝he, Holdes wirkend, sie m├╢gen ruhn im Stall, bei uns sich labend; Die bunten m├╢gen reich hier sein an K├дlbern, an vielen Morgen Milch dem Indra gebend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra grants the desires of the man who offers to him sacrifice and praise; he ever bestows upon him wealth, and deprives him not of that which is his own; again and again increasing his riches, he plural ces the devout man in an inaccessible fortress.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Abhinna khilye: ┼Ыatrubhirabhetavye, not to be breached by enemies;

Khilye = khila, normally wasteland, but here it means apratihatasth─Бnam, an unassailed or unassailable plural ce, one which is unapproachable by others, gantuma┼Ыakye sthale

Jamison Brereton

Indra does his best for the man who sacrifices and delivers in full. He gives more; he does not steal what belongs to him.
Making wealth increase more and more just for him, he establishes the man devoted to the gods in undivided virgin land.

Jamison Brereton Notes

What precise kind of land ├бbhinne khily├й refers to is unclear; see disc. by Oldenberg and Geldner n. 2d. The general opinion is that ├бbhinne (тАШuncut, unsplitтАЩ) describes land that hasnтАЩt been broken into parcels, but I wonder if it instead means тАШunploughedтАЩ – that is, unsplit by a plough.

Griffith

Indra aids him who offers sacrifice and gifts: he takes not what is his, and gives him more thereto.
Increasing ever more and ever more his wealth, he makes the pious dwell within unbroken bounds.

Geldner

Indra will dem, der opfert und schenkt, n├╝tzlich sein; er gibt ihm noch dazu, aber raubt nicht seine Habe. Immer mehr seinen Reichtum vergr├╢├Яernd setzt er den Gottergebenen in ein ungeteiltes Brachland.

Grassmann

Indra schenkt Gut dem opfernden und spendenden; er theilt ihm mit und entzieht ihm nicht das Seine; indem er stets aufs neue seinen Besitz mehrt, gibt er dem Frommen ungetrenntes Weideland.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet not the dust-spurning (war) horse reach them nor let them fall in the way of sacrificial consecration let the cattle of the man who offers sacrifice wander about at large and without fear.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Not let them fall: na saс╣Гskс╣Ыtatram abhyupayanti = vi┼Ыasan─Бdisaс╣Гsk─Бdisaс╣Гsk─Бram n─Бbhyupagacchantu, let them not go right to the consecration of immolation; as metonymy, perhaps the cows means their produce, milk and butter, which are constantly offered

Jamison Brereton

No dusty-necked steed gets to them (in a cattle raid), nor do they go to the place for dressing [=slaughterhouse].
The cows of the mortal who sacrifices wander far across wide-ranging (space) free of fear.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On reс╣З├║-kak─Бс╣нa- see EWA s.v. kak─Б╠Бс╣нik─Б-, kс╣Ы╠Бk─Бс╣нa-. Some part of the back of the head/neck is meant. What exact threat the dusty-necked steed poses to the cows isnтАЩt exactly clear. S─Бyaс╣Зa. explains ├бrv─Б as yuddh─Бrtham ─Бgato тАШ┼Ыvaс╕е. I would limit the тАЬintent to fightтАЭ more narrowly to a cattle raid, but there is no further evidence to bring to bear. See immed. below.

saс╣Гskс╣Ыtatr├бm is also somewhat problematic. It is generally referred to the root тИЪkс╣Ыt тАШcutтАЩ (see AiG II.2.170 and, most recently, EWA p. 316 s.v. KART1 ), but this affiliation is disputed by Whitney (Roots, p. 23) and, most vigorously, by Oldenberg, who assigns it to тИЪkс╣Ы for both formal and semantic reasons. The standard rendering is тАШSchlachtbankтАЩ (slaughter or, Whitney [AV, despite Rts], slaughterhouse). Against this interpr., Oldenberg makes the reasonable point that in this pre-ahiс╣Гs─Б era thereтАЩs no reason why a cow-owner wouldnтАЩt have his cows slaughtered when he wanted to.

But OldenbergтАЩs own solution is excessively convoluted and requires that the final -trabelong to тИЪtr─Б тАШprotectтАЩ, which seems dubious. (On gotr├б- and other possible forms of the thematized root noun -tr─Б╠Б- in compounds, see Scarlatta [194-95].) To meet OldenbergтАЩs objections, we can interpr. the clause in the context of the preceding clause and of the whole vs. The 2nd half of the vs. expresses a wish for the safety of cows that roam widely, presumably not always under the control and in the sight of a herdsman.

The first hemistich mentions several misadventures that could befall these roving cattle. P─Бda a refers, if IтАЩm right, to a cattle raid conducted by horsemen – what in the Oldenberg West (or at least the Oldenberg West of the imagination) would be called rustlers. It may be that the тАЬdusty neckтАЭ of the horse in question indirectly indicates that the horse is not a well-cared-for beast of the ─Аrya elite, or else that the raid requires hard riding in rough country. The second p─Бda may indicate that the cattle rustled were taken for meat or, under a different scenario, that the cows wandered into territory controled by tribals, non-─Аrya, or even non-elite ─Аrya (all without access to horses) who would ambush, kill, and eat them. Both p─Бdas would imply that the cattle are far from the safety of their home and enclosure.

My тАЬplace for dressingтАЭ reflects the possibility (see above) that saс╣Гskс╣Ыtabelongs to тИЪkс╣Ы not тИЪkс╣Ыt, and is a euphemistic expression for slaughter. However, if it does belong to тИЪkс╣Ыt тАЬтАж for slaughterтАЭ would be just fine.

The word order in p─Бda b is somewhat aberrant. The fem. pl. subj. t─Б╠Б(с╕е) occurs right after the verb, followed by the preverb abh├н, which ends the p─Бda: x x x x x, ├║pa yanti t─Б╠Бabh├н. We would ordinarily expect the pronoun t─Б╠Б(с╕е) to occur early in the clause (cf. p─Бda a #n├б t─Б╠Б(с╕е) [=3a]) and the preverb to precede the rest of the verbal complex. The word order disturbance may have been caused by the need to fit the bulky 4-syllable s├бс╣Гskс╣Ыtatram into the p─Бda, since it wonтАЩt fit the Jagat─л cadence.

Griffith

The charger with his dusty brow o’ertakes them not, and never to the shambles do they take their way.
These Cows, the cattle of the pious worshipper, roam over widespread pasture where no danger is.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDo you, cows, give us nourisment; render the emaciated, the unlovely body the reverse; do you, whose lowing is auspicious, make my dwelling prosperous; great is the abundance that is attributed to you in religious assemblies.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bс╣Ыhad vo vaya ucyate sabh─Бsu, great of you the food is said in assemblies; or, great is the food given to you in assemblies, it is given by all, sarvair d─лyate ityarthaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

You fatten even the thin man, o cows. You make even one without beauty to have a lovely face.
You make the house blessed, o you of blessed speech. Your vigor is
declared loftily in the assemblies.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs., like 5c, has an echo from the 2nd Maс╣Зс╕Нala: the final p─Бda bс╣Ыh├бd vo v├бya ucyate sabh─Б╠Бsu тАЬYour vigor is declared loftily in the assembliesтАЭ strikingly resembles the Gс╣Ыtsam─Бda Triс╣гс╣нubh refrain br╠еh├бd vadema vid├бthe suv─л╠Бr─Бс╕е тАЬMay we speak loftily at the ritual distribution, in possession of good heroes.тАЭ Both begin with adverbial bс╣Ыh├бt and contain a verb of speaking – a passive in our case – and a loc. of the place where the speech is spoken: vid├бthe тАШat the ceremony of distributionтАЩ, sabh─Б╠Бsu тАШin assembliesтАЩ, with sabh─Б╠Б- probably inhabiting a lower register, as might be appropriate for cows.

Kulikov (-ya-pres., 214) denies a passive value for ucyate here and tr. тАЬYour energy sounds loudly in the assembliesтАЭ for reasons that donтАЩt seem sufficient to me.

Griffith

O Cows, ye fatten e’en the worn and wasted, and make the unlovely beautiful tolook on.
Prosper my house, ye with auspicious voices. Your power is glorified in our assemblies.

Geldner

Ihr K├╝he machet selbst den Mageren fett, selbst den Unsch├╢nen machet ihr sch├╢n von Aussehen. Ihr machet das gesegnet, ihr mit gesegneter Stimme. Eure hohe Lebensst├дrkung wird in den Versammlungen verk├╝ndet.

Grassmann

Ihr K├╝he machet fett sogar den magern, den h├дsslichen auch macht ihr sch├╢n von Antlitz, Ihr macht begl├╝ckt das Haus, zum Gl├╝ck ert├╢nend, hoch wird ger├╝hmt eur Trunk bei den Gelagen.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпреВрдпрдореН) (рдЧрд╛рд╡рдГ) рд╡рд╛рдЪрдГ (рдореЗрджрдпрдерд╛) рд╕реНрдиреЗрд╣рдпрде рд╕реНрдирд┐рдЧреНрдзрд╛ рдордзреБрд░рд╛рдГ рдХреБрд░реБрддред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕рдВрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рдХреГрд╢рдореН) рдХреНрд╖реАрдгрдореН (рдЪрд┐рддреН) (рдЕрд╢реНрд░реАрд░рдореН) рдЕрд╢реНрд▓реАрд▓рдордордЩреНрдЧрд▓рдордзрд░реНрдорд╛рдЪрд░рдгрдореН (рдЪрд┐рддреН) рдЕрдкрд┐ (рдХреГрдгреБрдерд╛) рдХреБрд░реБрдеред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдкрд┐ рд╕рдВрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рддреАрдХрдореН) рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдХрд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рддреАрддрд┐рдХрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛рджреАрдирд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдВрд╕реНрддрдореН (рднрджреНрд░рдореН) рднрдиреНрджрдиреАрдпрдВ рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдХрд░рдВ рд╢реБрджреНрдзрд╡рд╛рдпреВрджрдХрд╡реГрдХреНрд╖рдореН (рдЧреГрд╣рдореН) (рдХреГрдгреБрде) (рднрджреНрд░рд╡рд╛рдЪрдГ) рдпрд╛ рднрджреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдХрд░реНрдпрдГ рд╕рддреНрдпрднрд╛рд╖рдгрд╛рдиреНрд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдЪрд╢реНрдЪ рддрд╛рдГ (рдмреГрд╣рддреН) рдорд╣рддреН (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рд╡рдпрдГ) рдЬреАрд╡рдирдореН (рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ) (рд╕рднрд╛рд╕реБ) рдЖрдкреНрддреИрд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рдирд╛рд╕реБ рееремрее
